text:
Loved the result, but I altered the recipe. I used 3 large bananas, 1/4 c oil and 1 cup applesauce (unsweetened) in place of the margarine.  I used 4 rounded T of instant cofee disolved in just a litte more that 1 T water, only 1 cup of sugar, and 1/4 cup egg beaters in place of the egg. I made the large muffins and baked them for about 35 minutes, then left them in the oven to cool with the door open.  They turned out very moist, and the flavor was wonderful...and low-fat!

text:
I was looking for a recipe to make banana muffins with the over ripe bananas I had. I found the best recipe ever!!!! I read all the reviews for this recipe and did make a few changes that were suggested. I used 1/4c marg and 3/4c applesauce instead of the full cup of Marg., I used half white and half brown sugar but only used 1 cup total, 3 tbsp coffee in 2 tbsp water,1 1/2 c whole wheat & 3/4 c white flours and I added 2 tsp ground flax seed. They turned out very yummy!! Will definitely make again.

text:
These are really good.  I followed the advice of others and added extra coffee - a good choice.  Instead of adding the full 1 cup of chocolate chips to the batter, I added 3/4 of a cup and used the rest of the cup to sprinkle on top along with chopped walnuts.  This made for quite a presentation.  Next time I might use less chocolate chips in the batter as the muffins were a bit sweet.  Overall a great muffin recipe.  Thanks Shelley.

text:
Made these for my husband, he gives them five out of five stars.  To cut down on fat & calories I made a few changes to the recipe:  I used 1/4 cup of margarine and 1 cup of unsweetened applesauce.  I used 3/4 cup sugar and used splenda to substitute for 1/2 cup of sugar.  In place of the water I used some unsweetened soy milk I had leftover to use up.  This batch almost made 2 pans of mini muffins.  I have a convection oven and baked them @ 350 for 15 min. 

Update Sept-2014:  I make this recipe all the time and I find it's very versatile.  I usually substitute with 1 cup of applesauce and 2 tablespoons of margarine or oil.  Also, I find you can easily sneak in 1/2 cup of cooked pureed carrots/peas - if you do that, just add a little bit more flour.  Also, this recipe works nicely using white whole wheat flour in place of regular flour.

I made these a little "lighter" for my family. I used whole wheat white flour, used butter instead of margerine (I don't keep margerine on hand often)and added an extra half-cup of mashed banana in place of some of the butter and I cut the sugar down to a scant 1/3 cup. These turned out very well, quite moist actually though they aren't one of our favorites. It's not because of the adjustments made--it's just the combination of the banana, chocolate and coffee. My kids and I just didn't care for it. My husband enjoyed these though, eating four in one sitting.

text:
YUM!  we inhaled these!   We did tweak it a bit:  a) Upped it to 6 tsp of coffee in 6 tsp of water. I was a bit worried it'd ruin the texture but it was fine. And you could actually taste the coffee.  b) Added in almost an entire packet of chocolate chips-they melted just so for a perfect yummy-ness.   And just as a warning they do come out very brown (i mean c'mon, it's 6 tsp of coffee here!) They're not ugly but they don't look like the picture. More like chocolate cupcakes.
I usually give 4 stars if I make a drastic change but these are so amazing I can't bring myself to it. I practically will my bananas to get yucky so I can make these; they've become my go-to muffins, I make them ALL the time.

text:
This recipe is a nice change from the same old banana muffin recipes. I did make some slight changes: substituted 3/4 cup unsweetened applesauce and 1/4 cup butter for the 1 cup margarine; reduced 1 1/4 cups white sugar to 1/2 cup and added 1/2 cup brown sugar; and used instant espresso coffee. I baked these in 2 mini muffin pans and baked for about 15 minutes. They came out moist and delicious. These are my new favorite mini muffins. Thanks for the recipe. I will make this again for sure.

text:
Good muffins. Pretty sweet. Like other reviewers, I added less sugar-about a cup, upped the coffee a bit, and made them with half butter, half oil. I wanted the flavor from the butter and the moisture from the oil (they were not dry at all this way). The butter kind of makes them taste like chocolate chip cookies in a muffin. They rose beautifully and are very attractive. I was out of brown sugar so I used all white, but I think brown in combo with the butter and mini chips would make them even more like chocolate chip cookies. The only thing I'm not sure about is the combination of the three flavors. I love coffee and chocolate, and I love banana and chocolate. I'm just not sure that the three together are not a little too distracting for my taste. I wonder if subbing cocoa for the coffee would solve this problem for me.

I didn't care for these, even though my family members and a co-worker enjoyed them.  I followed the suggestions of other reviewers and added 3 tbsp. instant coffee.  I also added extra mini chocolate chips because I love chocolate.  I do enjoy banana bread and I thought the coffee taste overpowered the banana. Thanks for the recipe! UPDATE (1/27/16): I've made these numerous times, and my kids love them. It's my new "go to" recipe when I have over-ripe bananas to use up. I was pleasantly surprised with this recipe. I guess you can't mess up making these..I used a hodge-podge of ingredients upon the suggestions of others in place of the margarine, including part pumpkin puree from the freezer and part applesauce amounting to almost 1 c in addition to 1/4 c oil. Also used 3 bananas from the freezer (you know how they look awful after awhile, all brown and syrupy)--I was glad for the coffee ingredient (which I tripled) just for the sake of appearance. It really dominated the final product so you'd better like mocha. I'm generally not a fan of coffee (dunno what I was expecting) so I think I might try just plain cocoa powder instead next time.  I did NOT taste the banana, which I missed. Otherwise, I was very pleased with the results after 22 min in the oven-17 good-sized, moist, decadent, teddybear-brown muffins.  P.S. I've not been thrilled with silicone bakeware in the past, but for muffins you can't beat it: no muffin papers, easy to clean, cools quickly so you can almost remove the muffins with bare hands. Try it!

These are very good muffins but have to only give them 4 stars because as the ingredients stand, the mocha or coffee flavor cannot be tasted. I doubled the amount of coffee and still couldn't taste it, nor could my husband. I combined suggestions from two different other reviews. This is what I did. I used 1/4 c. veg. oil and 1 c. unsweetened applesauce in place of the butter/margaine. I decreased the amount of sugar (good thing) to 1 c. but used 1/2 c. white and 1/2 c. dark brown. I used 3 med. bananas because that is what I had and put in 2 T. instant coffee in 2 T. of water. And I added 2 tsp. of flax seeds. Those are the only changes I made. The rest was the same. They are very chocolatey so I may even decrease the choc. chips to 3/4 c. But they are very moist. They do have flavor just not the mocha flavor that the title of the recipe states. I had the idea of using mocha chips next time. I think I have to order those online. I made some big muffins and some mini muffins (baked for 11 minutes) .I will make these again.

I will definately make these again!! I think next time I might try adding some flaked coconut.

text:
Excellent recipe. The title should omit the mocha part; the coffee works in it, but is not a strong flavor at all (I used 1 shot of Starbucks espresso). I also used a 9x13 pan instead of muffin cups, and it worked; the bread had a beautiful top and was perfect after 25-27 minutes. I used 1c. butter, the original amount of sugar, and added some extra chocolate chips (less than 1/4 cup) and sprinkled some on top, which made for a very nice mix of flavors. NOTE: If you do not have a large food processor, use a hand mixer, not a blender. Just make sure to process the bananas well first (in a small food processor or with the mixer; I used very ripe, pretty brown peeled bananas, which mashed well) and use soft butter, and you'll be fine - just make sure you get all the lumps out at the end. Check this one out, even if you don't like bananas normally!

text:
Before making these muffins, I read all of the other reviews.  After following the recipe to a tea, I added two more tablespoons to the coffee directions and dissolved it in three tablespoons of hot water, then added in to the mix.  This did make the batter a little thin,  but in the end,  they were great.  The only thing that I would do differently is fill the miffin cups almost to the top.  After filling the cups about 3/4 full, once they were baked, they  didn't have a good round top, next time I will fill the muffin cups more.  The muffins didn't rise as much as I thought they would.  Everything else remained the same.
This is a great after-school snack.

A tip for mashing bananas: just mush them while they're still in their skin -- no extra dirty dishes :) The peel might split a little, but you can keep on mushing them up.

text:
I followed the advice given by those who tried the recipe earlier by using 1/4c grapeseed oil+1c applesauce instead of butter or margarine. Grapeseed oil is odorless and can withstand higher cooking temperature compared to olive oil so it is better for baking. Added walnuts for extra crunch.The bitterness of walnuts helped to counteract on the sweetness of semi-sweet choc chips. And a dash of cinnanmon for frangrance. I only used 1 1/2 tbsp of coffee granules with 1tbsp of water so the coffee frangrance and taste wasn't overpowering. However, I sense there is something still missing in terms of ingreditent to add that extra oomp. Maybe I shoulded have used 1 to 1.5 tsp of cinnamon to bring out the frangrance. Just haven't quite found out what it is yet. Set the oven at 180degrees for about 25-30min in a fanforced oven with heating element working both the top and bottom of the oven. If heat is only kept at the top element, then the top of the muffins will turn cardboardy in texture and worst get burnt before the muffin is cooked in the inside. Great recipe regardless, and I will use it again.

text:
Absolutely fantastic! 

Instead of butter or margarine, I used 1 cup of apple sauce (home made by boiling 5 chopped medium sized apples in 3 Tsp of water and mashing it), and 4 level tsps of instant Nescafe coffee, dissolved in 3 tsp water, 3/4 cup of sugar.  Didn't have choco chips, so left it out. Kept in my bread bin in the fridge overnight so that it wouldn't stick to the paper cups. The 23 cakes vanished in less than 2 days. I could fainlty smell coffee (in spite of 4 tsp added) but the taste didn't stand out. 

The second time, I used 6 medium sized bananas for more moisture, in the first batch, mixed the choco chips, but it melted in the mixture, didn't spoil the taste though. In the second batch, I sprinkled the chips on top. Oh yes, added 5 tsp of coffee this time for a stronger coffee taste.

DELICIOUS.....

region:

country:
None
text:
At the risk of being scolded by those who don't like it when we made changes, I made a few change to these and they came out perfect. I think they would have been a 5 star without the changes, but here's what I did:
1.  Reduced butter to 1 stick (never use margarine)
2.  Used 3/4 cups of granulated sugar and 1/2 cup brown sugar.  
3.  Upped the amount of vanilla to 1 tbsp
4.  Added 1/2 cup sour cream in place of the second stick of butter 
5.  Added 1 cup of finely chopped pecans
6.  Instead of instant coffee, used 1 tbsp expresso granules.  No water needed, just added to the batter.

I did the normal creaming of the fats with the sugars, then used a whisk to combine flour and other dry ingredients to get some air into this mix.  Used a mixer instead of a food processor.  Then made 60 mini muffins.

they were good the first date, but try to wait for them to cool completely.  The next day they are super moist and just can't stop eating them.

for those on weight watchers, my modified recipe is 3 points per muffin.

text:
My husband, son and parents all raved about how moist and tasty these are!  I followed the directions exactly and loved the ease of mixing them up in the food processor.  I started with cold butter and it still worked perfectly.  I will likely try adding a couple tablespoons more of coffee next time as no one mentioned the mocha flavor -- just the banana/chocolate.  Also, I used an ice cream scoop to fill my lined muffin tin and got a full 1 1/2 dozen from this recipe.  One of my tins is dark coated, so I reduced the temperature in the over by 25 degrees.  Those came out a little lighter in color than the others, which were a bit dark for my liking.  That being said, no one complained!  I'll definitely watch them more closely next time I bake them.  Can't wait to try them myself!  Thanks for a great recipe.

text:
Some of the alterations I made are: I used 1 stick of butter and 1/2 cup of sweetened applesauce, 1 Tbs of regular and 1Tbs of decaf instant coffee dissolved in 1.5 Tbs water, 1 cup white sugar and 1/4 cup brown sugar. I added a small handful of slivered almonds. Before I added the chocolate chips and almonds, I stirred them in a little flour so they wouldn't fall to the bottom of the muffins. I used a blender for the first part but the flour wasn't mixing in it, so I poured the liquid into the flour and stirred the rest by hand. I made 18 regular sized muffins and took them out after 22-23 minutes. They are so moist and I really like the flavor. I will make these again.

text:
I scaled to 30 servings because I had 5 bananas to use up. I halved the margarine and sugar. Doubled the coffee granules and dissolved it in hot espresso. I changed the leavening to 1 tsp of baking powder and 1/4 tsp baking soda to each cup of flour used. I used Robing Hood Whole Wheat and Flax Omega 3 flour for the all purpose.  I added 1/4 tsp cinnamon to make it more like a cappuccino banana muffin, used dark chocolate chips as well. My #50 scoop made 30 muffins, which baked in 25 minutes at 375 degrees. Nice change from regular banana muffins, but even with doubling the coffee flavour is not at all evident.

These were great! I did make some changes, though. text:
Really good recipe. They turned out really moist and yet fluffy on the inside, and tastes so much better than the ones we get from bakeries!  Amount of bananas is just right but I find it a little too sweet for my family's liking. I reduced the sugar to only 170g and it was great. Halfed the amount of chocolate (used bittersweet instead) and for the other half, I substituted with pecans instead. Just make sure not to overmix as it will render the muffins too dense. I mixed everything using a non-electric hand whisk instead as I feel I can control the amount of mixing better. Just make sure to stop mixing when everything just combines. This is definitely a keeper!

text:
I feel like I'm being a little generous by giving this recipe four stars..The muffin tastes exactly like banana bread, which I guess is to be a little expected, but I honestly could have found a better banana bread recipe. I didn't even get a hint of coffee and I put about 5 tbsps of already-brewed coffee in it. The muffin itself is attractive, but that wasn't really what I cared about. I took other peoples advice and did a combo of white and brown sugar; also I used only butter. ALSO (this was a big deal breaker for me) the dough was SO thick! My food processor was too small for all the ingredients so at the point of adding flour and such I started mixing by hand; before adding flour, the butter was nasty looking (which I guess could be my fault) and it was such a turn off. After adding all the ingredients I decided to let it sit in the fridge for a few hours, however I became occupied and I ended up baking them the next day. The dough didn't get any less thick but they did bake well. I won't be making these again, which saddens me for I had high hopes for this recipe.

Baking the muffins went by really fast and it was really fun. I never baked muffins before so it was a first experience for me. The things that went well was making the lab plan and following it. The procedure was really clear and easy to follow. The outcome of the muffin was really similar to the pictures on recipe.com. The thing we forgot to do was read the materials because we ended up needing a food processor but didn't have one so we had to improvise and use a different mixer. Something I would do differently is change the amount of bananas because using two made it taste like straight up banana. The final product looked like an actual muffin, and it mushroomed up. I would recommend this to anybody who wants to try new things or likes bananas because this fits right in, and it is really fun to make and watch it bloom in the oven.

I do not think it's fair to rate this recipe as written because I followed the advice of other reviewers and changed the recipe a bit.  I reduced the sugar and used 1/2 c. white and 1/2 c. brown, substituted 1/2 cup unsweetened applesauce for 1/2 cup of margarine and used 1/2 c. butter instead of margarine.  I also used 3 Tbls of fresh-brewed strong coffee as I do not have any instant.  Just before baking, I added a mix of chocolate chips and crushed pecans to the top of the muffins.  They were delicious! Moist and tasty.  The coffee flavor was mild, to say the least, but still a tasty recipe.  Again, I cannot comment on the recipe as written, but with the suggestions mentioned, this recipe is a keeper!

text:
You won't need another banana chocolate chip muffin recipe.  Don't know if they're the best muffins ever, but these are good.  Made by hand; mixed the first batch of ingredients with a fork and then stirred in the flour batch.  (Mashed the bananas first, of course.)  Only complaint is that I got a chunk of coffee flavour here and there, maybe dissolve the granules in a bit more water.  Used 3/4 cup chocolate chips and 1/4 peanut butter chips - peanut butter and banana - mmm.  Butter instead of margarine due to what was on hand.
